## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of time and velocity. The absence of position as a separate variable suggests velocity-dependent nonlinear forces (damping/driving) and possibly explicit time-dependent forcing or that position is implicitly encoded via sinusoidal time dependence.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (viscous damping force proportional to velocity)
- Nonlinear (cubic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping with restoring force via time)
- Harmonic restoring via time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v (position as sinusoidal function of time plus damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 + c2 * v**2) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (velocity-dependent nonlinear term plus restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (time-modulated velocity coupling)
- Duffing-like with time: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 + c3 * v (cubic restoring force in position expressed via time)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v * abs(v) + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (drag proportional to v²)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (polynomial velocity dependence with harmonic restoring)
- Limit cycle form: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (self-sustained oscillation structure)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * sin(c3 * t) + c4 * v (parametric excitation)
- Simple forced: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (pure sinusoidal acceleration implying harmonic motion)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Velocity-dependent damping nonlinearity → odd-power polynomials in v (v, v³, v⁵) preserve symmetry of the oscillator
- Restoring force without explicit position variable → sinusoidal functions of time sin(ω*t) substitute for position in steady-state oscillation
- Self-excited oscillation (limit cycles) → terms of form (1 - v²)*v or v*(c₀ + c₁*v²) indicate amplitude-limiting mechanisms
- Phase-shifted harmonic components → sin(c*t + φ) or combinations of sin and cos at same frequency capture phase relationships
- Nonlinear oscillators with odd symmetry → acceleration function should be odd in state variables, restricting to odd powers of v
- Frequency mixing in nonlinear systems → products like v*sin(ω*t) indicate parametric or multiplicative coupling between velocity and driving
- Superharmonic content → presence of sin(n*ω*t) terms with integer multiples indicates nonlinear distortion of fundamental oscillation
- Energy-dependent frequency → terms coupling v² with trigonometric functions of t suggest amplitude-dependent frequency shifts
